				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Inc.">AT&amp;T Inc.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the company known as AT&amp;T since 2005. For the original AT&amp;T (American Telephone and Telegraph) founded in 1885, see <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T Corporation</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="AT&amp;T (disambiguation)">AT&amp;T (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Southwestern Bell Corporation" redirects here. For the telephone company founded in 1882, see <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Bell" title="Southwestern Bell">Southwestern Bell</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>AT&amp;T Inc.</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Whitacre_Tower" title="Whitacre Tower">Whitacre Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Dallas" title="Downtown Dallas">Downtown Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jbodonkor_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jbodonkor-5">[5]</a></sup> It is the world's largest telecommunications company, the largest provider of <a href="/wiki/Mobile_telephone" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile telephone">mobile telephone</a> services, and the largest provider of <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">fixed telephone</a> services in the United States through <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Communications" title="AT&amp;T Communications">AT&amp;T Communications</a>. Since June 14, 2018, it is also the parent company of mass media conglomerate <a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">WarnerMedia</a>, making it the world's largest media and entertainment company in terms of revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, AT&amp;T is ranked #9 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a></span>19.953 billion  (2018)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Asset" title="Asset">Total assets</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a></span>531 billion     (2018)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a></span>193.884 billion (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">251,840 (2019)<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Division_(business)" title="Division (business)">Divisions</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Communications" title="AT&amp;T Communications">AT&amp;T Communications</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/WarnerMedia" title="WarnerMedia">WarnerMedia</a></li><li><a href="#AT&amp;T_Latin_America">AT&amp;T Latin America</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Xandr" title="Xandr">Xandr</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Internet_Services" title="AT&amp;T Internet Services">AT&amp;T Internet Services</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://about.att.com">about<wbr></wbr>.att<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>AT&amp;T began its history as <b><a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Bell_Telephone_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Southwestern Bell Telephone Company">Southwestern Bell Telephone Company</a></b>, a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/Bell_Telephone_Company" title="Bell Telephone Company">Bell Telephone Company</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a> in 1877. The Bell Telephone Company became the <b>American Telephone and Telegraph Company</b> in 1885 and was later rebranded as <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T Corporation</a>. The 1982 <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_v._AT%26T" title="United States v. AT&amp;T">United States v. AT&amp;T</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> lawsuit resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Bell_System_divestiture" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell System divestiture">divestiture</a> of AT&amp;T Corporation's ("Ma Bell") subsidiaries or <a href="/wiki/Regional_Bell_Operating_Companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Bell Operating Companies">Regional Bell Operating Companies</a> (RBOCs), commonly referred to as  "Baby Bells", resulting in several independent companies, including Southwestern Bell Corporation; the latter changed its name to <b>SBC Communications Inc.</b> in 1995. In 2005, SBC purchased its former parent AT&amp;T Corporation and took on its branding, with the merged entity naming itself AT&amp;T Inc. and using its history, iconic logo and stock-trading symbol. In 2006, AT&amp;T Inc. acquired <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a>, the last independent Baby Bell company, making its formerly joint venture <a href="/wiki/Cingular" class="mw-redirect" title="Cingular">Cingular Wireless</a> (which had acquired AT&amp;T Wireless in 2004) wholly owned and rebranding it as <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">AT&amp;T Mobility</a>.
</p><p>The current AT&amp;T <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_the_Bell_System#Evolution_of_the_Baby_Bells" title="Breakup of the Bell System">reconstitutes much of the former Bell System</a>, and includes ten of the original 22 Bell Operating Companies along with the original <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Communications" title="AT&amp;T Communications">long distance division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Origin_and_growth_.281885.E2.80.931981.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_and_growth_(1885–1981)">Origin and growth (1885–1981)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origin and growth (1885–1981)" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Origins" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Origins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Monopoly" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Monopoly</a></div>
<p>AT&amp;T traces its origins to the Bell Telephone Company, founded by Alexander Graham Bell, <a href="/wiki/Gardiner_Greene_Hubbard" title="Gardiner Greene Hubbard">Gardiner Greene Hubbard</a>, and Thomas Sanders after Bell's patenting of the telephone.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> One of that company's subsidiaries was the American Telephone and Telegraph Company (AT&amp;T), established in 1885,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> which acquired the Bell Company on December 31, 1899, for legal reasons, leaving AT&amp;T as the main company. AT&amp;T established a network of subsidiaries in the United States and Canada that held a phone service <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a>, authorized by government authorities with the <a href="/wiki/Kingsbury_Commitment" title="Kingsbury Commitment">Kingsbury Commitment</a>, throughout most of the twentieth century. This monopoly was known as the <a href="/wiki/Bell_System" title="Bell System">Bell System</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and during this period, AT&amp;T was also known by the nickname Ma Bell.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> For periods of time, the former AT&amp;T was the world's largest phone company.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Breakup_and_reformation_.281982.E2.80.932004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakup_and_reformation_(1982–2004)">Breakup and reformation (1982–2004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Breakup and reformation (1982–2004)" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_the_Bell_System" title="Breakup of the Bell System">Breakup of the Bell System</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Post_break-up_restructuring" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Post break-up restructuring</a></div>
<p>In 1982, U.S. regulators <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_the_Bell_System" title="Breakup of the Bell System">broke up the AT&amp;T monopoly</a>, requiring AT&amp;T to divest its regional subsidiaries and turning them each into individual companies. These new companies were known as Regional Bell Operating Companies, or more informally, Baby Bells.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> AT&amp;T continued to operate long distance services, but as a result of this breakup, faced competition from new competitors such as <a href="/wiki/MCI_Communications" title="MCI Communications">MCI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a>.
</p><p>Southwestern Bell was one of the companies created by the breakup of AT&amp;T Corp. The architect of divestiture for Southwestern Bell was Robert G. Pope. The company soon started a series of acquisitions. This includes the 1987 acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Metromedia" title="Metromedia">Metromedia</a> mobile business and the acquisition of several cable companies in the early 1990s. In the latter half of the 1990s, the company acquired several other telecommunications companies, including some Baby Bells, while selling its cable business. During this time, the company changed its name to SBC Communications. By 1998, the company was in the top 15 of the Fortune 500, and by 1999 the company was part of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> (lasting through 2015).
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Purchase_of_former_parent_and_acquisitions_.282005.E2.80.932014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Purchase_of_former_parent_and_acquisitions_(2005–2014)">Purchase of former parent and acquisitions (2005–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Purchase of former parent and acquisitions (2005–2014)" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Rise_of_SBC" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Rise of SBC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Post-consolidation_wireless_acquisitions" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Post-consolidation wireless acquisitions</a></div>
<p>In 2005, SBC purchased AT&amp;T for $16 billion. After this purchase, SBC adopted the better-known AT&amp;T name and brand, with the original AT&amp;T Corp. still existing as the long-distance landline subsidiary of the merged company. The current AT&amp;T claims the original AT&amp;T Corp.'s history (dating to 1885) as its own. However, it retains SBC's 1983-2005 corporate structure.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> It also retains SBC's pre-2005 stock price history, on the company's website there is also historical date for all AT&amp;T companies and subsidiaries.
</p><p>In September 2013, AT&amp;T Inc. announced it would expand into <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> through a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_M%C3%B3vil" title="América Móvil">América Móvil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In December 2013, AT&amp;T announced plans to sell its Connecticut wireline operations to Stamford-based <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Communications" title="Frontier Communications">Frontier Communications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Recent_developments_.282014.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments_(2014–present)">Recent developments (2014–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent developments (2014–present)" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_AT%26T#Recent_developments" title="History of AT&amp;T">History of AT&amp;T § Recent developments</a></div>
<p>AT&amp;T purchased the Mexican carrier <a href="/wiki/Iusacell" class="mw-redirect" title="Iusacell">Iusacell</a> in late 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-androidcentral.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-androidcentral.com-17">[17]</a></sup> and two months later purchased the Mexican wireless business of <a href="/wiki/NII_Holdings" title="NII Holdings">NII Holdings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> merging the two companies to create <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mexico" title="AT&amp;T Mexico">AT&amp;T Mexico</a>.
</p><p>In July 2015, AT&amp;T purchased <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> for $48.5 billion, or $67.1 billion including assumed debt,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> subject to certain conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> AT&amp;T subsequently announced plans to converge its existing U-verse home internet and IPTV brands with DirecTV, to create AT&amp;T Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>On October 22, 2016, AT&amp;T announced a deal to buy Time Warner for $108.7 billion in an effort to increase its media holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-discucssesideaholdings_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discucssesideaholdings-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asutotoincrease_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asutotoincrease-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-advancedtalksa_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-advancedtalksa-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>AT&amp;T also owns approximately a 2% stake in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a>-domiciled entertainment company <a href="/wiki/Lionsgate" title="Lionsgate">Lionsgate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ATTinvestment_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATTinvestment-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>On July 13, 2017, it was reported that AT&amp;T would introduce a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud-based</a> <a href="/wiki/Digital_video_recorder" title="Digital video recorder">DVR</a> streaming service as part of its effort to create a unified platform across DirecTV and its <a href="/wiki/DirecTV_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="DirecTV Now">DirecTV Now</a> streaming service, with <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_U-verse" title="AT&amp;T U-verse">U-verse</a> to be added soon.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In October 2018, it was announced that the service would launch in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Named <a href="/wiki/HBO_Max" title="HBO Max">HBO Max</a>, the service's release date was pushed to 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>On September 12, 2017, it was reported that AT&amp;T planned to launch a new cable TV-like service for delivery over-the-top over its own or a competitor's broadband network sometime next year.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>On November 20, 2017, Assistant Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Makan_Delrahim" title="Makan Delrahim">Makan Delrahim</a> filed a lawsuit for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice_Antitrust_Division" title="United States Department of Justice Antitrust Division">United States Department of Justice Antitrust Division</a> to block the merger with Time Warner, saying it "will harm competition, result in higher bills for consumers and less innovation."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In order for AT&amp;T to fully acquire Time Warner, the Department of Justice stated that the company must divest either DirecTV or <a href="/wiki/Turner_Broadcasting_System" title="Turner Broadcasting System">Turner Broadcasting System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, AT&amp;T is the world's largest telecommunications company.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> AT&amp;T is also the largest provider of mobile telephone <sup id="cite_ref-AT&amp;T_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT&amp;T-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Verizon_Wireless_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Verizon_Wireless-44">[44]</a></sup>  services and the largest provider of <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">fixed telephone</a> services in the United States. 
<sup id="cite_ref-LRG_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRG-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>On March 7, 2018, the company prepared to sell a minority stake of <a href="/wiki/DirecTV_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="DirecTV Latin America">DirecTV Latin America</a> through an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">IPO</a>, creating a new holding company for those assets named Vrio Corp.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> However, on April 18, just a day before the public debut of Vrio, AT&amp;T canceled the IPO due to market conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>On June 12, 2018, AT&amp;T was given permission by U.S. District Court Judge <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Leon" title="Richard J. Leon">Richard J. Leon</a> to go ahead with its $85 billion deal for Time Warner. The DOJ had attempted to stop the merger fearing it would harm competition.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The merger closed two days after, becoming a wholly owned subsidiary and division of AT&amp;T with a new name, WarnerMedia, announced the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>Three months after completing the acquisition, AT&amp;T reorganized into four main units: Communications, including consumer and business wireline telephony, AT&amp;T Mobility, and consumer entertainment video services; WarnerMedia, including Turner cable television networks, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> film and television production, and <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>; AT&amp;T Latin America, consisting of wireless service in Mexico and video in Latin America and the Caribbean under the <a href="/wiki/Vrio_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vrio (company)">Vrio</a> brand; and Advertising and Analytics, since renamed <a href="/wiki/Xandr" title="Xandr">Xandr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-otp.tools.investis.com_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otp.tools.investis.com-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>By 2019, AT&amp;T had developed partnerships with <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> providers to develop <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things#Medical_and_healthcare" title="Internet of things">mobile health-related connectivity devices</a> that aid inpatient care. Key products include a telemetry device that monitors patient metrics, while toggling between WIFI and cellular connectivity.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2019, <a href="/wiki/Activist_investor" class="mw-redirect" title="Activist investor">activist investor</a> <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Management_Corporation" title="Elliott Management Corporation">Elliott Management</a> revealed that it had purchased $3.2 billion of AT&amp;T stock (a 1.2% equity interest), and had pushed for the company to divest assets to improve its share value.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>On March 4, 2020, AT&amp;T announced its intent to perform major cost-cutting moves, including cuts to capital investment, and plans to promote <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_TV" title="AT&amp;T TV">AT&amp;T TV</a> (which officially launched nationally on March 2) as its primary pay television service offering. AT&amp;T will still primarily promote DirecTV "where cable broadband is not prevalent", and as a specialty option.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span id="AT.26T_Latin_America"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="AT&amp;T_Latin_America">AT&amp;T Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: AT&amp;T Latin America" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">

class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.att.com/">www<wbr></wbr>.att<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p><b>AT&amp;T Latin America</b> (formerly <b>AT&amp;T International, Inc.</b>) is a wholly owned division of AT&amp;T which operates in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and 11 countries in Latin America and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>In 2017, AT&amp;T announced a new AT&amp;T International corporate division housing AT&amp;T Mexico, DirecTV Latin America and their stakes of <a href="/wiki/SKY_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="SKY Brazil">SKY Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky Mexico">Sky Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2016, AT&amp;T announced a deal to acquire <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a> worth $85.4 billion (including assumed Time Warner debt). The proposed deal would give AT&amp;T significant holdings in the media industry; AT&amp;T's competitor <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> had previously acquired <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a> in a similar bid to increase its media holdings, in concert with its ownership of television and internet providers. If approved by federal regulators, the merger would bring Time Warner's properties under the same umbrella as AT&amp;T's telecommunication holdings, including satellite provider DirecTV.<sup id="cite_ref-AT&amp;T_Deal_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT&amp;T_Deal-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>By the end of July, the company announced that, effective August 1, a new structure was created before the acquisition would close. On September 15, 2017, Reuters reported, citing anonymous sources, that AT&amp;T, the owner of DIRECTV's U.S. and Latin American divisions, had hired an advisor to consider offering AT&amp;T Latin America on the public stock market. In November 2017, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">U.S. Justice Department</a> said it was moving to sue to block the AT&amp;T-Time Warner merger.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On November 20, 2017, the Department of Justice filed an antitrust lawsuit over the acquisition; Makan Delrahim stated that the deal would "greatly harm American consumers". AT&amp;T asserts that this suit is a "radical and inexplicable departure from decades of antitrust precedent".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> On December 22, 2017, the merger agreement deadline was extended to June 21, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On April 19, 2018, the IPO was cancelled. On June 12, 2018, the AT&amp;T-Time Warner merger was approved by a federal judge.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Two days later, AT&amp;T completed the acquisition of Time Warner, and a day later the company was renamed WarnerMedia.
</p><p>On September 21, 2018, AT&amp;T reclassified it four principal divisions which include AT&amp;T International which now have some assets moved out like the RSNs, and also merging Consumer Mobility, Technology, and Business Mobility and renamed the company as AT&amp;T Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-otp.tools.investis.com_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otp.tools.investis.com-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Landline_operating_companies">Landline operating companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Landline operating companies" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Of the eight companies that were part of the Breakup of the Bell System, these five are a part of the current AT&amp;T:<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ameritech" title="Ameritech">Ameritech</a>, acquired by SBC in 1999</li>
<li>AT&amp;T Corp., acquired by SBC in 2005</li>
<li>BellSouth, acquired by AT&amp;T in 2006</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pacific_Telesis" title="Pacific Telesis">Pacific Telesis</a>, acquired by SBC in 1997</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Bell" title="Southwestern Bell">Southwestern Bell</a>, rebranded as <a href="/wiki/SBC_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="SBC Communications">SBC Communications</a> in 1995</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span id="Chart_of_AT.26T_Baby_Bells"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_of_AT&amp;T_Baby_Bells">Chart of AT&amp;T Baby Bells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chart of AT&amp;T Baby Bells" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table style="border-spacing: 0px; border-collapse: separate; font-size:75%;"><tbody><tr style="height:1px;text-align:center"><td colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="height:2em;width:2em"></td><td colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="height:2em;width:2em"></td><td colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="height:2em;width:2em"></td><td colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="height:2em;width:2em"></td><td colspan="6" rowspan="2" style="border:2px solid black;padding:0.2em"><a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T Corporation</a><br><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/RBOC" style="border:2px solid black;padding:0.2em"><a href="/wiki/CenturyLink" title="CenturyLink">CenturyLink</a></td><td colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="height:2em;width:2em"></td></tr><tr style="height:1px;text-align:center"></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_operating_companies">Former operating companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Former operating companies" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The following companies have become defunct or were sold under SBC/AT&amp;T ownership:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Southern_New_England_Telephone" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern New England Telephone">Southern New England Telephone</a>: sold to Frontier Communications in 2014<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Woodbury_Telephone" title="Woodbury Telephone">Woodbury Telephone</a>: merged into Southern New England Telephone on June 1, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_of_rural_landlines">Decline of rural landlines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Decline of rural landlines" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Of the <a href="/wiki/Baby_Bell" class="mw-redirect" title="Baby Bell">Baby Bells</a>, Ameritech sold some of its <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a> landlines to <a href="/wiki/CenturyTel" class="mw-redirect" title="CenturyTel">CenturyTel</a>, in 1998; BellSouth sold some of its lines to MebTel, during the 2000s; <a href="/wiki/US_West" title="US West">U S WEST</a> sold many historically Bell landlines to Lynch Communications and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Telecom" title="Pacific Telecom">Pacific Telecom</a>, in the 1990s; <a href="/wiki/Verizon" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon">Verizon</a> sold many of its <a href="/wiki/Verizon_New_England" title="Verizon New England">New England</a> lines to <a href="/wiki/FairPoint_Communications" title="FairPoint Communications">FairPoint</a>, in 2008, and its <a href="/wiki/Frontier_West_Virginia" title="Frontier West Virginia">West Virginia</a> operations to Frontier Communications, in 2010.
</p><p>On October 25, 2014, Frontier Communications took over control of the AT&amp;T landline network in Connecticut after being approved by state utility regulators. The deal was worth about $2 billion, and included Frontier inheriting about 2,500 of AT&amp;T's employees and many of AT&amp;T's buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structure">Corporate structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate structure" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AT%26TOrange.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/AT%26TOrange.JPG/220px-AT%26TOrange.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/AT%26TOrange.JPG/220px-AT%26TOrange.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AT%26TOrange.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>AT&amp;T office in <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a>, Texas</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities_and_regions">Facilities and regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Facilities and regions" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>The company is headquartered at Whitacre Tower in <a href="/wiki/Downtown" title="Downtown">downtown</a> Dallas, Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-Jbodonkor_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jbodonkor-5">[5]</a></sup> On June 27, 2008, AT&amp;T announced that it would move its corporate headquarters from downtown San Antonio to <a href="/wiki/One_AT%26T_Plaza" class="mw-redirect" title="One AT&amp;T Plaza">One AT&amp;T Plaza</a> in downtown Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-Jbodonkor_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jbodonkor-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The company said that it moved to gain better access to its customers and operations throughout the world, and to the key technology partners, suppliers, innovation and human resources needed as it continues to grow, domestically and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> AT&amp;T Inc. previously relocated its corporate headquarters to San Antonio from St. Louis, Missouri, in 1992, when it was then named Southwestern Bell Corporation. The company's Telecom Operations group, which serves residential and regional business customers in 22 U.S. states, remains in San Antonio.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Atlanta, Georgia, continues to be the headquarters for AT&amp;T Mobility, with significant offices in Redmond, Washington, the former home of <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Wireless_Services" title="AT&amp;T Wireless Services">AT&amp;T Wireless</a>. Bedminster, New Jersey, is the headquarters for the company's Global Business Services group and AT&amp;T Labs and is where the original AT&amp;T Corp. remains located. St. Louis continues as home to the company's Directory operations, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Advertising_Solutions" class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Advertising Solutions">AT&amp;T Advertising Solutions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>AT&amp;T offers also services in many locations throughout the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia Pacific</a>; its regional headquarters is located in Hong Kong.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The company is also active in Mexico, and on November 7, 2014, it was announced that Mexican carrier Iusacell would be acquired by AT&amp;T.<sup id="cite_ref-androidcentral.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-androidcentral.com-17">[17]</a></sup> The acquisition was approved in January 2015.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> On April 30, 2015, AT&amp;T acquired wireless operations Nextel Mexico from NII Holdings (now AT&amp;T Mexico).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Corporate governance" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Randall_Stephenson,_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Randall_Stephenson%2C_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg/220px-Randall_Stephenson%2C_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Randall_Stephenson%2C_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg/220px-Randall_Stephenson%2C_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Randall_Stephenson,_CEO_of_AT%26T.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CEO <a href="/wiki/Randall_L._Stephenson" title="Randall L. Stephenson">Randall L. Stephenson</a> at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a></div></div></div>

<p>The current management as of October 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> includes:<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Randall L. Stephenson – <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> (CEO)</li>
<li>Angela Santone- <a href="/wiki/Chief_administrative_officer" title="Chief administrative officer">chief administrative officer</a> (CAO)</li>
<li>William A. Blase, Jr. – <a href="/wiki/Senior_executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior executive vice president">senior executive vice president</a> of <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a></li>
<li>John J. Stephens – <a href="/wiki/Senior_executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior executive vice president">senior executive vice president</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">chief financial officer</a> (CFO)</li>
<li>David S. Huntley – <a href="/wiki/Senior_executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior executive vice president">senior executive vice president</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chief_compliance_officer" title="Chief compliance officer">chief compliance officer</a></li>
<li>David R. McAtee II – <a href="/wiki/Senior_executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Senior executive vice president">senior executive vice president</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_counsel" title="General counsel">general counsel</a></li>
<li>Lori Lee – CEO of AT&amp;T Latin America and global marketing officer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Stankey" title="John Stankey">John Stankey</a> – president and COO of AT&amp;T Inc., CEO of WarnerMedia</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_involvement">Political involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Political involvement" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Responsive_Politics" title="Center for Responsive Politics">Center for Responsive Politics</a>, AT&amp;T was the fourteenth-largest donor to United States federal political campaigns and committees from 1989 to 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-osorghh2011_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osorghh2011-83">[83]</a></sup> having contributed more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$84.1 million</span>, 58% of which went to <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> and 42% of which went to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a>. As an example, in 2005, AT&amp;T was among 53 entities that contributed the maximum of $250,000 to the second inauguration of President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-drinkard2005_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drinkard2005-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usatoday25may2008_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday25may2008-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP25may2005_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP25may2005-86">[86]</a></sup> Bill Leahy, representing AT&amp;T, sits on the Private Enterprise Board of the <a href="/wiki/American_Legislative_Exchange_Council" title="American Legislative Exchange Council">American Legislative Exchange Council</a> (ALEC).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> ALEC is a <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">nonprofit organization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">state legislators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> representatives that drafts and shares model state-level legislation for distribution among state governments in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fcir_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcir-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>During the period of 1998 to 2019, the company expended <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$380.1 million</span> on <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-osorgatt2019_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osorgatt2019-91">[91]</a></sup> A key political issue for AT&amp;T has been the question of which businesses win the right to profit by providing broadband internet access in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-osorgatt2007_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osorgatt2007-92">[92]</a></sup> The company has also lobbied in support of several federal bills. AT&amp;T supported the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission_Process_Reform_Act_of_2013_(H.R._3675;_113th_Congress)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Communications Commission Process Reform Act of 2013 (H.R. 3675; 113th Congress)">Federal Communications Commission Process Reform Act of 2013 (H.R. 3675; 113th Congress)</a>, a bill that would make a number of changes to procedures that the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Federal_Communications_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Federal Communications Commission">U.S. Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) follows in its rulemaking processes.<sup id="cite_ref-3675cbo_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3675cbo-93">[93]</a></sup> The FCC would have to act in a more transparent way as a result of this bill, forced to accept public input about regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-PeteVotesTransparency_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeteVotesTransparency-94">[94]</a></sup> AT&amp;T's Executive Vice President of Federal Relations, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tim_McKone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tim McKone (page does not exist)">Tim McKone</a>, said that the bill's "much needed institutional reforms will help arm the agency with the tools to keep pace with the Internet speed of today's marketplace. It will also ensure that outmoded regulatory practices for today's competitive marketplace are properly placed in the dustbin of history."<sup id="cite_ref-ATTblog_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATTblog-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2018, reports emerged that AT&amp;T made 12 monthly payments between January and December 2017 to Essential Consultants, a company set up by President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s lawyer <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cohen_(lawyer)" title="Michael Cohen (lawyer)">Michael Cohen</a>, totaling $600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Although initial reports on May 8 mentioned only four monthly payments totaling $200,000,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> documents obtained by the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> on May 10 confirmed the figure of 12 payments, which had begun three days after the President was <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Inauguration of Donald Trump">sworn into office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-99">[99]</a></sup> AT&amp;T confirmed the report the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-100">[100]</a></sup> The report from the <i>Washington Post</i>, as well as additional reporting from <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_News" title="Bloomberg News">Bloomberg</a>, revealed the payments had been made for Cohen to "provide guidance" relating to the attempted $85 billion merger with <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-99">[99]</a></sup> to gain information on the Trump administration's planned tax reforms, as well as about potential changes to <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality_in_the_United_States" title="Net neutrality in the United States">net neutrality</a> policies under the new FCC.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> However, Chairman of the FCC <a href="/wiki/Ajit_Pai" title="Ajit Pai">Ajit Pai</a> denied Cohen ever inquired about net neutrality on AT&amp;T's behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> A spokesperson for AT&amp;T said that the company had been contacted by <a href="/wiki/Special_Counsel_investigation_(2017%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Counsel investigation (2017–present)">the Special Counsel investigation led by Robert Mueller</a> regarding the payments, and had provided all the information requested in November and December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>In early 2019, the Democratic <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_the_Judiciary" title="United States House Committee on the Judiciary">House Judiciary</a> requested records related to the AT&amp;T-Time Warner merger from the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_financial_performance">Historical financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Historical financial performance" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>The financial performance of the company is reported to shareholders on an annual basis and a matter of public record. Where performance has been restated, the most recent statement of performance from an annual report is used.<sup id="cite_ref-AR-2015_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR-2015-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AR-2014_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR-2014-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10K_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-109">[109]</a></sup></p>

<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hemisphere_database">Hemisphere database</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hemisphere database" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hemisphere_Project" title="Hemisphere Project">Hemisphere Project</a></div>
<p>The company maintains a database of <a href="/wiki/Call_detail_record" title="Call detail record">call detail records</a> of all telephone calls that have passed through its network since 1987. AT&amp;T employees work at <a href="/wiki/High_Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area" title="High Intensity Drug Trafficking Area">High Intensity Drug Trafficking Area</a> offices (operated by the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_National_Drug_Control_Policy" title="Office of National Drug Control Policy">Office of National Drug Control Policy</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> so data can be quickly turned over to law enforcement agencies. Records are requested via an administrative subpoena, without the involvement of a court or grand jury.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Censorship" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In September 2007, AT&amp;T changed its legal policy to state that "AT&amp;T may immediately terminate or suspend all or a portion of your Service,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> any Member ID, electronic mail address, IP address, Universal Resource Locator or domain name used by you, without notice for conduct that AT&amp;T believes ... (c) tends to damage the name or reputation of AT&amp;T, or its parents, affiliates and subsidiaries."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> By October 10, 2007, AT&amp;T had altered the terms and conditions for its Internet service to explicitly support freedom of expression by its subscribers, after an outcry claiming the company had given itself the right to censor its subscribers' transmissions.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Section 5.1 of AT&amp;T's new terms of service now reads "AT&amp;T respects freedom of expression and believes it is a foundation of our free society to express differing points of view. AT&amp;T will not terminate, disconnect or suspend service because of the views you or we express on public policy matters, political issues or political campaigns."<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy_controversy">Privacy controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Privacy controversy" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg/220px-Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2646" data-file-height="1980"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg/220px-Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Page9-SER_klein_exhibits.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diagram of how alleged wiretapping worked. From <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">EFF</a> court filings<sup id="cite_ref-kleinex_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kleinex-114">[114]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/NSA_call_database" class="mw-redirect" title="NSA call database">NSA call database</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Klein" title="Mark Klein">Mark Klein</a>, <a href="/wiki/NSA_warrantless_surveillance_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="NSA warrantless surveillance controversy">NSA warrantless surveillance controversy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hepting_v._AT%26T" title="Hepting v. AT&amp;T">Hepting v. AT&amp;T</a></div>
<p>In 2006, the Electronic Frontier Foundation lodged the <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> lawsuit <i>Hepting v. AT&amp;T</i>, which alleged that AT&amp;T had allowed agents of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a> (NSA) to monitor phone and Internet communications of AT&amp;T customers without warrants. If true, this would violate the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Intelligence_Surveillance_Act" title="Foreign Intelligence Surveillance Act">Foreign Intelligence Surveillance Act</a> of 1978 and the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Fourth Amendments</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Constitution">U.S. Constitution</a>. AT&amp;T has yet to confirm or deny that monitoring by the NSA is occurring. In April 2006, retired former AT&amp;T technician Mark Klein lodged an <a href="/wiki/Affidavit" title="Affidavit">affidavit</a> supporting this allegation.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The Department of Justice has stated it will intervene in this lawsuit by means of <a href="/wiki/State_Secrets_Privilege" class="mw-redirect" title="State Secrets Privilege">State Secrets Privilege</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2006, the United States District Court for the Northern District of California – in which the suit was filed – rejected a federal government motion to dismiss the case. The motion to dismiss, which invoked the State Secrets Privilege, had argued that any court review of the alleged partnership between the federal government and AT&amp;T would harm national security. The case was immediately appealed to the Ninth Circuit. It was dismissed on June 3, 2009, citing retroactive legislation in the Foreign Intelligence Surveillance Act.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> reported that all international and domestic calling records had been handed over to the National Security Agency by AT&amp;T, Verizon, SBC, and BellSouth for the purpose of creating a massive <a href="/wiki/NSA_call_database" class="mw-redirect" title="NSA call database">calling database</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The portions of the <i>new</i> AT&amp;T that had been part of SBC Communications before November 18, 2005, were not mentioned.
</p><p>On June 21, 2006, the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> reported that AT&amp;T had rewritten rules on its privacy policy. The policy, which took effect June 23, 2006, says that "AT&amp;T – not customers – owns customers' confidential info and can use it 'to protect its legitimate business interests, safeguard others, or respond to legal process.'"<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>On August 22, 2007, National Intelligence Director <a href="/wiki/John_Michael_McConnell" title="John Michael McConnell">Mike McConnell</a> confirmed that AT&amp;T was one of the telecommunications companies that assisted with the government's warrantless wire-tapping program on calls between foreign and domestic sources.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p><p>On November 8, 2007, Mark Klein, a former AT&amp;T technician, told <a href="/wiki/Keith_Olbermann" title="Keith Olbermann">Keith Olbermann</a> of <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a> that all Internet traffic passing over AT&amp;T lines was copied into <a href="/wiki/Room_641A" title="Room 641A">a locked room</a> at the company's San Francisco office – to which only employees with National Security Agency clearance had access.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>AT&amp;T keeps for five to seven years a record of who text messages whom and the date and time, but not the content of the messages.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>AT&amp;T has a one star <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">privacy</a> rating from the Electronic Frontier Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Intellectual_property_filtering">Intellectual property filtering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Intellectual property filtering" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2008, the company reported plans to begin filtering all <a href="/wiki/Internet_traffic" title="Internet traffic">Internet traffic</a> which passes through its network for intellectual property violations.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu-125">[125]</a></sup> Commentators in the media have speculated that if this plan is implemented, it would lead to a mass exodus of subscribers leaving AT&amp;T,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> although this is misleading as Internet traffic may go through the company's network anyway.<sup id="cite_ref-Wu_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wu-125">[125]</a></sup> Internet freedom proponents used these developments as justification for government-mandated <a href="/wiki/Network_neutrality" class="mw-redirect" title="Network neutrality">network neutrality</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrimination_against_local_Public-access_television_channels">Discrimination against local Public-access television channels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Discrimination against local Public-access television channels" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>AT&amp;T has been accused by <a href="/wiki/Community_media" title="Community media">community media</a> groups of discriminating against local <a href="/wiki/Public,_educational,_and_government_access" title="Public, educational, and government access">Public, educational, and government access</a> (PEG) cable TV channels, by "impictions that will severely restrict the audience".<sup id="cite_ref-dn10_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn10-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>According to Barbara Popovic, Executive Director of the Chicago public-access service <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Access_Network_Television" title="Chicago Access Network Television">CAN-TV</a>, the new AT&amp;T <a href="/wiki/U-verse" class="mw-redirect" title="U-verse">U-verse</a> system forced all <a href="/wiki/Public-access_television" title="Public-access television">Public-access television</a> into a special menu system, denying normal functionality such as channel numbers, access to the standard <a href="/wiki/Program_guide" class="mw-redirect" title="Program guide">program guide</a>, and DVR recording.<sup id="cite_ref-dn10_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn10-127">[127]</a></sup> The Ratepayer Advocates division of the <a href="/wiki/California_Public_Utilities_Commission" title="California Public Utilities Commission">California Public Utilities Commission</a> reported: "Instead of putting the stations on individual channels, AT&amp;T has bundled community stations into a generic channel that can only be navigated through a complex and lengthy process."<sup id="cite_ref-dn10_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn10-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>Sue Buske (president of telecommunications consulting firm the Buske Group and a former head of the National Federation of Local Cable Programmers/<a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Community_Media" title="Alliance for Community Media">Alliance for Community Media</a>) argue that this is "an overall attack [...] on public access across the [United States], the place in the dial around cities and communities where people can make their own media in their own communities".<sup id="cite_ref-dn10_127-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn10-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_security">Information security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Information security" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In June 2010, a <a href="/wiki/Hacker_group" title="Hacker group">hacker group</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Goatse_Security" title="Goatse Security">Goatse Security</a> discovered a <a href="/wiki/Vulnerability_(computing)" title="Vulnerability (computing)">vulnerability</a> within AT&amp;T that could allow anyone to uncover email addresses belonging to customers of AT&amp;T 3G service for the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld1_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld1-128">[128]</a></sup> These email addresses could be accessed without a protective password.<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld2-2_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld2-2-129">[129]</a></sup> Using a script, Goatse Security collected thousands of email addresses from AT&amp;T.<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld1_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld1-128">[128]</a></sup> Goatse Security informed AT&amp;T about the security flaw through a third party.<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld2-1_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld2-1-130">[130]</a></sup> Goatse Security then disclosed around 114,000 of these emails to <a href="/wiki/Gawker_Media" title="Gawker Media">Gawker Media</a>, which published an article about the security flaw and disclosure in <i><a href="/wiki/Valleywag" title="Valleywag">Valleywag</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld1_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld1-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-computerworld2-1_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld2-1-130">[130]</a></sup> Praetorian Security Group criticized the web application that Goatse Security exploited as "poorly designed".<sup id="cite_ref-computerworld1_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld1-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2015, AT&amp;T was fined $25 million over data security breaches, marking the largest ever fine issued by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) for breaking data privacy laws. The investigation revealed the theft of details of approximately 280,000 people from call centres in Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Accusations_of_enabling_fraud">Accusations of enabling fraud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Accusations of enabling fraud" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unbalanced plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-unbalanced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">unbalanced</a> towards certain viewpoints</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit">improve the article</a> by adding information on neglected viewpoints, or discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:AT%26T" title="Talk:AT&amp;T">talk page</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>In March 2012, the United States federal government announced a lawsuit against AT&amp;T. The specific accusations state that AT&amp;T "violated the False Claims Act by facilitating and seeking federal payment for IP Relay calls by international callers who were ineligible for the service and sought to use it for fraudulent purposes. The complaint alleges that, out of fears that fraudulent call volume would drop after the registration deadline, AT&amp;T knowingly adopted a non-compliant registration system that did not verify whether the user was located within the United States. The complaint further contends that AT&amp;T continued to employ this system even with the knowledge that it facilitated the use of IP Relay by fraudulent foreign callers, which accounted for up to 95 percent of AT&amp;T's call volume. The government's complaint alleges that AT&amp;T improperly billed the TRS Fund for reimbursement of these calls and received millions of dollars in federal payments as a result."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Racism">Racism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Racism" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 28, 2015, AT&amp;T announced that it had fired Aaron Slator, President of Content and Advertising Sales, for sending racist text messages.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Slator was also hit with a $100 million discrimination lawsuit, filed by African-American employee Knoyme King.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The day before that, protesters arrived at AT&amp;T's headquarters in Dallas and its satellite offices in Los Angeles as well as at the home of CEO Randall Stephenson to protest alleged systemic racial policies. According to accounts, the protesters are demanding AT&amp;T begin working with 100% black-owned media companies.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Trademark_violation">Trademark violation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Trademark violation" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In June 2016, <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> sued AT&amp;T for <a href="/wiki/Trademark_infringement" title="Trademark infringement">trademark infringement</a>, <a href="/wiki/False_designation_of_origin" title="False designation of origin">false designation of origin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unfair_competition" title="Unfair competition">unfair competition</a>. The company had recently established a loyalty program under the brand <i>AT&amp;T Thanks</i>, which Citigroup claims would cause consumer confusion as an infringement of its "ThankYou" and "Citi ThankYou" marks due to similar wording and visual design. Citi, which also provides a co-branded <a href="/wiki/Credit_card" title="Credit card">credit card</a> for AT&amp;T that links with its ThankYou rewards program, sought unspecified damages and the expungement of AT&amp;T's trademark registration.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-thankyoutm_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-thankyoutm-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg-tylawsuit_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-tylawsuit-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>The suit was dismissed in August 2016, with a judge ruling that there was a low likelihood of confusion between the two marks because the companies fall within different industries and that consumers who use loyalty programs would be able to "clearly take into account the attributes associated with the products they purchase" and, thus, be able to distinguish them.<sup id="cite_ref-nyp-thankslawsuit_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyp-thankslawsuit-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_rights_and_sponsorships">Naming rights and sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Naming rights and sponsorships" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=AT%26T&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references"><li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/732717/000095012304012515/x67907e8vk.htm">Form 8-K</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190116200750/https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/732717/000095012304012515/x67907e8vk.htm">Archived</a> January 16, 2019, at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a>. <li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Svensson, Peter (September 29, 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://phys.org/news/2011-09-document-cos-private.html">"Document Shows How Phone Cos. Treat Private Data"</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190513134626/https://phys.org/news/2011-09-document-cos-private.html">Archived</a> from the original on May 13, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">May 13,</span> 2019</span>. <q>T-Mobile USA doesn't keep any information on Web browsing activity. Verizon, on the other hand, keeps some information for up to a year that can be used to ascertain if a particular phone visited a particular Web site. According to the sheet, Sprint Nextel Corp.'s Virgin Mobile brand keeps the text content of text messages for three months. Verizon keeps it for three to five days. None of the other carriers keep texts at all, but they keep records of who texted who for more than a year. The document says AT&amp;T keeps for five to seven years a record of who text messages who —and when, but not the content of the messages. Virgin Mobile only keeps that data for two to three months.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Document+Shows+How+Phone+Cos.+Treat+Private+Data&amp;rft.date=2011-09-29&amp;rft.aulast=Svensson&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fphys.org%2Fnews%2F2011-09-document-cos-private.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAT%26T" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
